Abolishing New Year Greetings

— Careful Words

The term "New Year greetings" itself, I feel, is fundamentally somewhat incomprehensible. "Year" is merely a marker for calculating time, twelve months accumulating into a year, as commonplace and unremarkable as ten decimeters making a meter. Why must it necessarily be celebrated? Based on my personal speculation, the reason people in the past had this whole New Year greeting ritual was perhaps a form of consolation or encouragement. The idea was that now is the start of another year, please forget the past and strive to open up a new chapter! However, judging from the actions of people today, it seems absolutely not for this purpose. Upon meeting, they always greet you with a heap of smiling "Congratulations," and in written correspondence, it's always the four characters "Happy New Year." I truly don't understand what valuable thing I gained from the Republic of China transitioning from the 22nd to the 23rd year that warrants everyone uniformly congratulating me? I can't even begin to fathom what official position or wealth my relatives and friends have collectively attained in this new year that necessitates me congratulating them one by one? Thinking about it, on the contrary, I feel that time passes so quickly, year after year, someone has already died, and a friend is growing old. I barely have time to offer condolences, how can I then shout "Congratulations" to them, heartlessly deceiving them? As for myself, I also understand very well that precious youth is about to be taken away by time. Although I can't quite say I'm old, almost every New Year gives me an indication, saying, "You are one step closer to the realm of old age!" That being said, all my relatives and friends should be expressing regret for me, why should they be celebrating for me?

As for saying that no one escapes death, even though nearing old age, as long as your career is progressing, it is worth celebrating. But I dare say that in this year, especially in China, you shouldn't even think about making any progress in any career, let alone hope for any progress. If you are not one to dare to use ruthless means and have not forgotten that there are still the two words "humanity" in the dictionary, I believe that no matter what New Year begins, it is merely a sign that your career will decline another step, and it is difficult to maintain the status quo, how can you even think of any progress?

Summarizing the above two points, the change of year is fundamentally just a milestone in the journey of life. With each passing year, one is one step closer to death, fundamentally something to be mourned and not celebrated. If it is for celebrating each other's career progress, in this year, it is even more of a dream. Therefore, I advocate, I firmly advocate, that the act of New Year greetings must be abolished immediately! If someone says that New Year greetings mean celebrating a new environment or a new atmosphere, then I hope they go to the Xianxia Ridge on the border of Fujian and Zhejiang on a windless day to listen to the sounds of cannons!

Three Excellences of Suzhou

— Yan Qiao

Mr. Gu Tinglin said, "People of the North, eat their fill all day, and have nothing to occupy their minds. People of the South gather in groups all day and do not speak of righteousness." Although this was said about the general scholars and officials of the late Ming and early Qing dynasties, looking at the people of the North and South today, they are still the same old way, without any improvement. Mr. Wang Yuyang said, "Wu Valley has three excellences: cockfighting, playing mahjong, and eating pufferfish, worshiping the Five Gods. Even scholars and officials cannot avoid this, I wish I had the Emperor's sword to execute those who started this." Although this was also a lament from over two hundred years ago, it can still be used after more than two hundred years. The only difference is that mahjong has been changed to general's cards. However, eating pufferfish often causes life-threatening problems, and people in Suzhou today dare not eat it anymore. The Five Gods, once banned by Tang Bin in the Qianlong era and then banned by Wang Yincai after the National Revolution, no longer have the same awe-inspiring power as before. Now, the only pastime for scholars and officials is mahjong and general's cards; even the ladies and grandmothers are unhappy without it. Wang Chuanshan said mahjong destroyed the Ming dynasty, I say mahjong and general's cards will destroy the [people], I don't think that's an overstatement.

Because the winning or losing of mahjong and general's cards is a small problem, the waste of energy and time is a big problem. Although those who play cards do so in their spare time and it does not hinder their work, once they enter the card game, everything else is abandoned, and they still have to discuss and study after the game. How can this invisible consumption be recorded with numbers?

As for eating, Suzhou people were originally the most particular about it. But now they are far inferior to Shanghai people, because Shanghai can be said to have everything, and there is nothing strange that they don't have. As long as there is blood, they can taste something new. However, people in Suzhou have recently continued to fall into the trap of opium, and many young people have become addicted to this habit. Soon, they will look haggard, which is thousands of times more poisonous than pufferfish.

As for worshiping gods, it is not the Five Gods, but the "modern god." Whether male or female, what they strive for all day is modernity. Especially those young people, even more unwilling to lag behind others at all. So, even if they talk about the national goods year, they don't care. If they talk about the year of national subjugation, they still want to be modern. Moreover, the modernity they seek is only material decoration. If Mr. Gu and Mr. Wang were alive today, how would they lament!

Stepfather

— Qing Qu

The two words "stepfather" are a vulgar and unbearable term. In fact, "slow" and "fast" are opposites, "fast" just took precedence, then "slow" just fell behind! Therefore, "stepfather," from a more refined term, is simply "stepfather," nothing strange. For example, a husband, his wife dies, and soon after, he marries another wife. The daughter born to his previous wife cannot but recognize her as "mother," and nominally calls her "stepmother." Then, a widow, her husband dies, and later, she marries another man as her husband, commonly known as "filling the room." But this widow is not single, she already has children when her previous husband was alive. What would these children call their mother's current husband? Then, even if the person herself cares about face and refuses to call him that, in the eyes of others, they always say in the same tone, he is her "stepfather"!

A few days ago, there was a Mr. Chen, I will conceal his name. He was already over thirty years old, and also married. At first, he did business in Shanghai, and was quite fortunate. He had savings of five or six thousand, so he enjoyed the blessings at home and didn't want to develop abroad, thinking of himself as a wealthy man. Little did he know that "sitting and eating, three years of sea will be empty." His family situation became worse day by day, so a sudden inspiration came, and unable to vent his anger, he actually picked up an ax to kill his "stepfather." This matter caused an uproar in the city, and it is not known how it will end. After the incident, he was caught and taken to the Public Security Bureau, and also transferred to the law. Originally, it was a bloody case, how could it be dealt with vaguely? Alas! Unexpectedly, there is a very interesting wonderful passage in the back, writing it out, it is also in the unreasonable, there is an emotional meaning, see it in this case!

A Mr. Chen, created the disaster of killing his "stepfather"! The "stepfather" was bleeding from his head and was operated on in the hospital, his life could be saved. But the knife-wielding murderer could not but be locked up in the detention center. At this time, his mother could not help but cry, saying, "My son killed my husband, now my husband is not dead, but my son is in jail, not only can I not face my son, but how can I face my previous husband? My son was born to my previous husband, now the one he killed is not my son's father, alas! The blame is on me, but I love my son, and I can't help but love my husband." So, she asked someone to persuade the murdered person to withdraw the lawsuit, and at the same time, thought of rescuing the criminal from prison. In the past, she looked at her "stepfather" like a stranger, but now her daughter and daughter-in-law go to the hospital to comfort him morning and evening, and affectionately call him "Daddy." According to this, the "stepfather" took a few knives, and actually made the name of father, and Mr. Chen borrowed a knife to issue a marriage certificate on behalf of his mother, is this not a very funny news story?

Random Notes

A beauty of unsurpassed charm is like a spring flower of brilliant red and purple. But the spring light fades easily, the spring color ages easily, and the spring flower also withers easily, hence beautiful women often have unfortunate lives.

A famous scholar with a belly full of learning is like the clear and bright autumn moon. But the autumn scenery is sparse, the autumn light fades easily, and the autumn moon also wanes easily, hence famous scholars often end up destitute.

The process of life is divided into three periods. The past is like the road-building period. The present is the period of opening to traffic. The future is the period of full speed. Speed ​​up the journey period.

The process of love is also divided into three periods. The past is the sweet period. The present is the tasteless period. The future is the bitter and spicy period.

The ancients had the elegant pastime of wandering at night with candles, seeking lines before flowers, and searching for poems in the moonlight. Today, under the bright electric lights, [there is no need to hold candles], or they make a bamboo forest tour, or engage in unruly behavior, staying up all night, doing their best, far different from the ancients' candlelit night tours.

— Exhaustively Stated

The Four Northeast Company Commanders

— Zhang Henshui

The Twenty-first Chapter: Under the Lamp, Bitterly Instructing a Weak Daughter-in-law; Wandering Down the Mountain, Coldly Observing a Hero

As for the words about gender equality and freedom to make friends, it's ultimately not good. Making friends is a matter for men, managing household affairs is the duty of those inside the bedroom. What good does making friends do? If people say you like freedom, that's not good. If they don't say that, then it's hard to say. Ah..." Jiang's spoke for a while, loaded with veiled accusations and dragging her feet. Guizhi, because she herself felt guilty about what she had done, how could she not understand? Her face became even redder, and she just sat there with her head lowered, folding and unfolding the two small newspapers on the table. Jiang's then knew that her words had hit Guizhi's sore spot, so she stopped saying anything, picked up the fabric in her arms, and sewed a few more stitches. But she only sewed a few stitches, then put it down again, and continued to talk to herself, "It's not that I'm being nagging, raising a daughter is the most difficult thing these days. If you're too strict, people will say you're stubborn and old-fashioned. But then again, in these times, you have to be strict. But if you relax a little, who knows what kind of trouble will arise. People these days have poisonous tongues. If it gets out of hand, they'll even put you in the newspaper." These words were heavier than what she had said before, and Guizhi's face was even redder, as if it had been smeared with pig's blood, even her eyelids were red. The two earrings hanging from her ears were shaking uncertainly. Jiang's glanced at her out of the corner of her eye, but didn't say anything, and lowered her head to work again. After Guizhi received these two criticisms from her mother, she knew that they were directed at her, but if she didn't say anything, it would be like admitting to the accusation. Although her mother was not an outsider, she thought that if she silently acknowledged her mother's words, it would be as if she really had some illicit affair, and that would be an injustice! So she deliberately put on an angry look, pushed the newspaper forward, and suddenly stood up, saying, "Aren't you making a joke? Listening to your tone, it's as if I have some unacceptable thing that you've seen. Isn't this what people call gossiping about others' families? But you're gossiping about your own family." (282)

New Year

— Yu Yangling

On Christmas Eve, many foreign men and women seen on Avenue Joffre were mostly merry. But there were also children who envied the toys in the splendid glass cabinets and refused to leave, only to be pulled away by their parents, and thus felt that the "universal celebration" was not yet here.

From the fact that foreigners celebrate Christmas like the Chinese celebrate the New Year, I thought about how we are also about to celebrate the New Year. But because I live in the city and am a bit older than a child, I no longer have much interest in celebrating the New Year. The most interesting New Year was always when I was a child living in the countryside.

There were so many things to do in the countryside. Starting from sending the Kitchen God to heaven on the twenty-third night, we entered the New Year holiday. From then on, the children had something to be merry about and something to eat every day, just without wearing new clothes. It was not the same for the adults. Although they also had something to be merry about and something to eat, in the days before the second New Year's Day, they still had to be busy and worried, especially on the last day of the year, collecting debts, paying debts, borrowing debts, and avoiding debts, it would always be noisy until three or four in the morning.

If it was a poor person who owed debts, then the last day of the year was an extremely difficult ordeal.

Scolding, beating, stripping clothes, robbing furniture... all kinds of shame and suffering were the homework that poor people could not escape on the last day of the year. They could only endure, endure until dawn.

Dawn was the first day of the New Year. However, strangely, the poor people who were scolded, beaten, stripped of their clothes, and had their furniture robbed because they could not repay their debts one or two hours ago, were now wearing a slightly less patched-up piece of clothing and going out, and there must be money hidden inside this piece of clothing, from several to dozens of yuan.

They took this money to gamble. Gambling was the only entertainment for poor people during the New Year, and for the first five days of the New Year, it was "imperial gambling," and no one would come to prohibit it. Taking advantage of this opportunity, they wanted to have as much fun as possible.

They didn't care about being scolded or beaten for not repaying debts, they didn't care about being stripped of their clothes or having their furniture robbed, they didn't even care about letting their wives and children go hungry, during the New Year season, the "gambling capital" had to be prepared no matter what.

Therefore, according to common sense, the poor people are really foolish and despicable.

However, the mood of the poor people who would rather suffer a little more of the usual hardships on the last day of the year in order to gamble for a few days of happiness in the year is not unimaginable. Everyone pursues happiness, [who differs in heart according to their poverty or success], but who can arrange things as comfortably as the rich?

However, the rich are always clever. They invented a method, which is to still collect debts on the morning of the first day of the New Year, but with lanterns lit, counting it as if the last day of the year had not yet passed, which did not violate the rules. But for the poor, it was a major misfortune.

What is said above is about celebrating the Lunar New Year, and may only be limited to my hometown. Since the Gregorian calendar was adopted, I don't know how the poor people in my hometown and other places are celebrating the New Year.

A Glimpse of [A History of Modern Chinese Literature]

— Yu Shixia

Recently, I bought Qian Jibo's [A History of Modern Chinese Literature]. However, the meaning of [modern] that Mr. Qian put on this book is different from ours, so the modern Chinese literature he is talking about is also different from ours. Opening the book, I saw his introduction. At the end of his introduction, he said, "Why not write Republic of China, but write modern? It is said that our Republic of China was created shallowly, and the writers who were temporarily promoted all had their heads exposed at the end of the late Qing Dynasty. Even the elders lived as if they didn't want to serve the orthodoxy of the Republic of China. How could one summarize it with the Republic of China! And another army was formed, rising after the founding of the Republic of China, only Zhang Shizhao's logic and Hu Shi's vernacular literature! Therefore, living in this world, talking about literature and only being limited to the Republic of China, this is a crime against literature!"

Originally, he titled the two words "modern" for the old remnants who [did not want to serve the Republic of China], and the literature he wanted to talk about was precisely the literature of this group of people. In the book, whenever he mentioned the Manchu Qing Dynasty, he called it [Late Qing], which was of course using the Spring and Autumn writing style used by historians since Confucius. As for his punctuation, he liked to use exclamation points, which was also of course the intention of Ouyang Gong's new Five Dynasties history, which liked to use [Alas]. Standing on this position, using this view, to look at modern Chinese literature, he naturally only saw the literature of the old remnants, and could not help but exclaim, "Living in this world, talking about literature and only being limited to the Republic of China, this is a crime against literature!"

Looking at the table of contents of this book again, the introduction and the beginning of the book, explaining literature, literary history, and the history of modern Chinese literature, generally discussing the changes in literature in the Middle Ages, occupy a total of forty pages. From the ancient literature in the upper volume to the so-called new literature [New People's Style] [Logical Essay] in the lower volume, it occupies 424 pages. When it comes to vernacular literature, from page 425 to page 449, there are only 29 pages. I thought that if he did not write this point about vernacular literature, wouldn't it be just right to title it "A History of Old Literature" or "Ancient Literature" of modern China? And there are already 424 pages, which is rich enough! If not, simply don't write the lower volume, and don't allow Liang Qichao's New People's Style and Zhang Shizhao's Logical Essay to be included in the book title and call it [A History of Modern Chinese Literature of the Old Generation] would be more appropriate. Although Zhang Taiyan is listed in it, it doesn't matter, because Mr. Zhang has already signed himself [Zhang Binglin, a remnant of the Republic of China] in a couplet to mourn Li Yuanhong. If the writing is for the sake of the pure and flawless style of this book, it is best to only write the upper volume, and kick Mr. Zhang away with one foot, and title it [A History of the Literature of the Late Qing Dynasty], wouldn't that be great? This old man is not smart, but wants to offer this humble opinion to the author Mr. Qian, I wonder what Mr. Qian thinks?

The modern Chinese vernacular literature seen by Mr. Qian has only one writer, Hu Shi, and only Zhou Shuren and Xu Zhimo are mentioned in the appendix, and only Guo Moruo, Yu Dafu, and Jiang Guangchi are mentioned by name.

After buying Qian's A Glimpse of a History of Modern Chinese Literature, I can't help but say a few words. After reading it through in the future, there may be a sequel.

A Brief Discussion on [Art] and [Artist]

— Tang Jun

There are people who, relying on their [intuition], use the combination of colors, lines, tones, or gestures as tools to constantly and maximally express their [self] and unfold their [life]. The more harmonious the combination of these colors, lines, tones, or gestures, the more vivid their [self] appears, and the more meaningful their [life] unfolds. The more meaningful and powerful their life unfolds, the more profound the [traces] of those unfoldings become. The easier it is for people to feel these [traces]. These traces - paintings, sculptures...etc, people give them a special name, calling them [art]. The person who makes this [unfolding of life] and [expression of self] is called the [artist].

The so-called [art] and [artist], on the easy side, we have seen and heard many such names in the West, really as common as everyday meals. A [singer], an [actor], people call him [artist]. The [songs] and [scripts] that they sing and perform, people call them [works of art]. Works related to painting, sculpture, decorative arts, etc., are also called [art], and the people who create these works are also called [artists]. Western Europeans in general do not have a more special concept of this name than other names. In China, it is not the same. People with [long hair] and [large bow ties] seem to feel that they are not enough to express that they are [artists]. Their desire to obtain the title of [artist] is more important than anything else. Hearing people call him [artist] is more glorious than anything else. These are all [morbid] manifestations of a nation with unhealthy [aesthetic consciousness] and a country with backward art.

On the difficult side, a work that has no [life], no [self], and expresses no power, although it is called [art] in name, has no artistic value in [content]. A person whose life is extremely ordinary, or who uses colors, lines, etc. to spend his life on a very ordinary path, although he has a large bow tie, long hair, and the [form] of an artist, has no [substance] of an artist.

Of course, riding in a car, living in a big house, taking concubines, being a military officer, and always having several soldiers with pistols following behind, these, in the minds of ordinary people, always seem to be a very meaningful life, but in the eyes of [artists], they are not worth looking at. On the other hand, the life of a savage on a desert island, living with savages, and playing with deer, has cast Gauguin's great [artistic life], has cast Gauguin's great [art], has cast Gauguin as such a great [artist]!

Small Notes from a Guest Window

— Shu

19

[You Zhengwei's Letters], three volumes, written by the Qing poet Wu Xiqi, contains two hundred and twenty letters, which can be said to be quite a lot in terms of quantity, but reading them is quite disappointing. Except for the early works in the first volume, they are all social articles and correspondence. Early letters are not large in quantity, but they are rich in authenticity, allowing readers to see his life, thoughts, and environment. In a letter to Jian Baogu, he said [We are extremely distressed people]. His early life was indeed like this. Xiqi replied to Xu Tieyai's letter, saying [The west wind is gradually cold, and all my cotton clothes are in pawn, I hope for some moisture to revive the difficulty]. He said to his younger brother Ruoyu, [The previous debt has not been paid off, and the later debt is coming again, I really don't know when I will be able to jump out of this troubled world]. He sent a letter to Yang Jintang, saying [My situation is that I am being tortured in bitterness every day... I want to return to sweetness, but I can't get it. The population in the family is gradually increasing, and the house is almost breaking. My sister's prospects are also declining day by day, and I have to cook without rice every morning]. The state of poverty can be seen most clearly in these letters. And this period of life is also the most unforgettable for him, so there is still such a memory in his later hand-written notes [It is not easy to live in Chang'an, and there are eight mouths to feed, with a hot pot on top of my head, I really don't know what to do]. (Sent to Zhao Caichen)

Two Brothers (7)(5)

— By Maupassant, Translated by Li Weike

Mother Roland asked:

"Has Pierre not come down?"

Her husband shrugged his shoulders and replied:

"No, let him be. He's always late. We can eat first."

She turned to Jean and said:

"You should go call him, my child. He'll be angry if we don't wait for him."

"Okay, Mom, I'll go."

So the young man ran out.

He went upstairs with the fervent determination of a timid person going into a fight.

When he knocked on the door, Pierre replied:

"Come in."

He entered.

The other was bent over the table writing.

"Good morning," Jean said.

Pierre stood up.

"Good morning."

So they shook hands as if nothing had happened.

"Aren't you coming down for breakfast?"

"But... because... I have a lot to do."

The older brother's voice trembled, his uneasy eyes seeming to ask what he should do.

"Everyone's waiting for you."

"Ah! Is... is our mother downstairs?"

"Downstairs, and she's the one who asked me to call you."

"Ah! Then... I'll go down."

Outside the dining room door, he hesitated, unwilling to enter first. Then, with a sudden gesture, he opened the door. He saw his father and mother sitting opposite each other across the dining table.

He looked at the ground and silently walked up to her. Like recently, he didn't kiss her cheeks but only bent down to offer his forehead for her to kiss. He guessed her mouth was near, but he didn't feel her lips touch his skin at all. He straightened up, his heart pounding after this pretense of affection.

He thought, "What did they say after I left last night?"

Jean constantly called out softly, "Mother," "Dear Mother," paying attention to her, serving her, pouring her drinks. Pierre then understood that they had cried together, but he couldn't penetrate their thoughts! Did Jean think his mother was guilty, or did he think his brother was despicable?

Shen Bao Amateur Weekly

Commentary

How to Utilize Spare Time?

— Zi Ming

With the development of the economic panic, the working hours of general occupational sectors are increasing day by day, so-called spare time is actually very little. Precisely because this time is very little, it is especially precious, and the handling of this precious time has become a very important issue.

Generally speaking, all people in work are immersed in hard, monotonous, and dry work every day, without any pleasure. Therefore, after finishing work, they will try their best to pursue entertainment, especially low-level entertainment, and waste a little precious time in playing mahjong, amusement parks, listening to storytelling, watching plays... and other low-level entertainment.

However, these low-level entertainments are the most likely to consume money and damage the spirit, and the most likely to make people increasingly degenerate. It is indeed a pity to waste a little precious spare time in such entertainment! Of course, we are tired all day long, and after work, we should find a little happiness to regulate this tired and dry life. But finding happiness does not necessarily mean indulging or being anesthetized in low-level entertainment, which is absolutely harmful to one's own spirit, one's future, and everything. In our spare time, we should look for more noble entertainment, that is, entertainment that does not harm our body and spirit, does not waste money, and can increase our knowledge. Under this principle, I hope that people of various occupations will properly improve their respective clubs and their family lives. At the same time, I also hope that the advanced members of the general society will pay attention to the issue of general entertainment, strive to promote relatively noble entertainment, and guide the lives of general workers. Our [Amateur Weekly] should especially bear a particularly important responsibility on this issue. In this way, it will not only be of great benefit to workers, clerks, teachers, ... all working people, but also of great benefit to the entire society.

However, I think the best thing to do in spare time is to read books and newspapers. This can increase our knowledge and is of great importance to society and to the individual's profession. Here, I think that the [Amateur Correspondence Reading Club] advocated by Mr. Xiaojie in the last issue of this magazine has a very important significance. If there is an opportunity in the future, I also plan to express some specific opinions on this.

Life

Environment and People

— A Er

Trainee

We two are sitting at the same desk, facing each other. But we are completely two people, two people who are different in everything...temperament, consciousness, work performance...are all different. We grew up in two different environments. Colorful environments create colorful people.

Originally, two people who are different in everything are not easy to stay together for a long time, and we will certainly be unable to avoid this, if not for the work we are doing together that connects us. In any case, that is only our superficial cooperation.

We both are trainees in the accounting department, doing the preliminary work in the accounting department...collecting invoices, sorting invoices, stapling invoices. I came in a few months earlier than him, so I know a little more. I told him everything I knew, but he was very casual about it.

Having money at home means that everything can be sloppy. This is the general opinion of young masters. He is a young master, so he agrees with this. He always runs in and out sitting in his shiny chartered car, which makes the wretched director who earns two or three hundred yuan a month and has to support a family of nine in Shanghai, and also has to maintain appearances, feel jealous. When he eats lunch, he complains that the food in the office is not good (that's two yuan a table, and I think that's already amazing!), so he adds an extra yuan every day. He has his hair permed once a week, BIGWAVE, which costs ten dimes each time. But he only has twenty old yuan a month (he doesn't care about this, and he once told me...he would rather not take a salary and be a dry clerk!). The wages he pays his driver every month are not enough! In addition, he often goes to the movies, no matter the size of the theater, if there is any [artistic] film or [nude beauty] dance, he is sure to go, no matter how far the theater is from his home.

In the eyes of rich fathers, a son like this is not considered too bad. He obeyed his father and married a wife chosen for him by his father when he was eighteen, and this year he had a daughter. (He is only twenty-one years old now!) Moreover, he denies some rich people's three major principles: no gambling, no prostitution, no opium. Just watching movies won't use up a mountain of wealth.

There are many people like him in Shanghai! I am the exact opposite of him. I am two years younger than him. I have a passionate and upward heart. The environment has made my form middle-aged. I understand that I should work, and my work performance must at least be balanced with the remuneration I receive (fifteen yuan). I think we must be the vanguard of the twentieth century and must not indulge in excessive enjoyment and luxury. In fact, I often cannot even satisfy the desire to buy a daily necessity. But I don't ask for it, I always think that there are still many poor people being trampled under our feet! (That is why I especially sympathize with the tea boys and old stewards in the office.) They began their training in hard labor while we had the privilege of going to paradise schools to study. This is certainly the failure of the old social system, but we cannot escape a part of the responsibility.

Because this young master does not feel any interest in the work and this work is not done by him alone, I always say to him with a smile...[Mr. Zhou, why don't you rest at home, why do you come here to do this kind of work?]

[ ! This kind of work is really annoying!]

He says this kind of work is annoying, but who knows that he has this attitude towards any kind of work? To be honest, I have never seen him be interested in a job. I think he must be prepared to live like this, all the way to the grave.

But, there are many powerful unemployed people crying out!

One Copper Coin Per Person

Two People Cooperate

— Yuan Xifu

Three Tenants

The cost of living in Shanghai is so high that I can't afford to live in a house alone, so I have to live in the back upstairs of a family with Mr. Huang from X University.

The cold wind was roaring on the horse sleep, the streetlights emitted a dim and yellow light, I felt a little cold, and after eating dinner in a small [basic goods] restaurant, I wanted to return to my room to read a book. There was no electric light on the stairs, and when I walked up, it was so dark that my tongue stuck out and couldn't find my mouth. After a long time, I touched the kerosene lamp that emitted light and accompanied me in the deep night, but for some reason, I struck seven or eight matches and it still didn't light. Using the short-term light of the matches, I saw that there was still half a lamp of oil. [There is oil, why doesn't it light?] I guessed to myself... [Maybe it's because of the lamp wick.] Another question popped up in my mind.

I had decided to buy a lamp wick to replace it, but when I touched the copper coins in my pocket, there was only one. A god of terror seemed to stand in front of my darkness, laughing at me. [What to do tonight? The landlord has gone out, and Mr. Huang has not yet returned. Sleep? I am unwilling to waste good time.] This kind of doubtful question was moving in my brain like an electric current.

The sound of footsteps on the stairs broke the silence in the room. I knew Huang had returned.

[Has the fire not been lit yet?] He asked this question as soon as he was halfway up the stairs.

[A lamp wick is broken, and I don't have money to buy it. I have to wait for you to come back!]

Page 20

[Don't you have even three copper coins? I only have one copper coin in my pocket.] He said slowly.

[I only have one in my pocket too.] I handed him a copper coin.

The two of us were silent for a while. Huang took the two copper coins and groped his way down the stairs. I sat silently on my bed, praying like a congregation in a church, hoping that God would forgive my sins.

After about twenty minutes, footsteps sounded on the stairs again. [I've bought it.] This was Huang's voice. When I heard the words [bought it], I jumped up as happily as a child getting a toy they had never seen before.

Relying on the short-term light of the match again, I replaced the new wick, and the dark little room was lit up again.

Current Affairs Research

The Headliner of the 1933 International Stage

— Di Lai

One of the most serious problems currently at the end of 1933 is the question of whether the League of Nations exists or not. This question has formed two camps, one supporting the League of Nations and the other reorganizing the League of Nations. The former is represented by Britain and France and their satellites, and the latter is represented by Italy, Germany, and their fellow travelers. It has become the center of European diplomatic struggles. London, Paris, Rome, and Berlin are stirring up huge waves.

The League of Nations is a beautiful term. What do the Chinese think of it? As long as we recall how the League of Nations handled the issue of the Three Eastern Provinces after September 18, we probably don't need to waste any more words! It was established in February 1919, after the Paris Spoils Conference. It was an organization led by Britain and France, with the participation of imperialist countries such as Italy and Japan, to carve up small and weak national colonies and suppress revolutions. However, it hung up a sign that [guaranteed international peace and protected labor] at its front door.

Over the past ten years, it has naturally fulfilled many of its historical missions, but it has not eased the contradictions between imperialist countries in any way. This political trust is changing and tending to shake with the contrast of economic and political forces between world imperialist countries, and it is reaching old age. After September 18, its inability to impose forceful sanctions on the destroyers of peace was already nakedly exposing its incompetence and deception to the public, and it had declared bankruptcy.

In this year when the world is comprehensively falling into a deeper economic panic and political crisis, the contradictions of capitalism and the opposition of imperialist countries have reached the point where they must be resolved by war. Old organizations need to be disbanded. Naturally, a comedy of support and overthrow must emerge from this decomposition.

The disintegration of the League of Nations was first due to Japan's withdrawal from the international community, and the League of Nations could do nothing about it. Now that the German fascists want to obtain the freedom of military adventure, they have also withdrawn from the League of Nations, and the League of Nations is equally unable to cope, and can only reduce its scope. This proves that the League of Nations has completely collapsed, and all activities based on the Geneva mechanism have completely disappeared in the eyes of the public.

Now the new force that has emerged is Fascist Italy, which is actively demanding the reorganization of the League of Nations, and Germany naturally holds the same view. Italy and Germany's opposition to the Versailles system is rooted in reason. Germany is the so-called victimized country, and Italy has not achieved a leading position in this. Italy is now demanding leadership in Europe. Germany has to strengthen its domestic dignity by means of adventurous foreign policies. Opposing the Treaty of Versailles and demanding equality in disarmament are the most pleasant demands. Using this as a threat to withdraw from the League of Nations and the Disarmament Conference is easy to dispel public dissatisfaction, dilute the tense emotions, and shift public attention. This is the basis of fascist diplomacy.

Italy and Germany are naturally the leaders of this camp. They want to smash this organization and change the division of European forces. They are waiting for war.

On the side of Britain and France, they are naturally not truly loving peace. It is just that they are unwilling to easily give up this established dominant force. Now they are coming out to defend the League of Nations, but it is just to prolong the time for everyone to prepare for war, and it may not be helpful to [world peace].

If we observe the comings and goings and collusion in Paris, France, the active communication with satellites, and the strengthening of their own forces, as well as the fervent discussions in London about the League of Nations and disarmament issues, with politicians, military experts, and pastors participating in the discussions, the scene is like the time when the Great War was about to begin in 1914, we can imagine that they are not afraid of war, they are also preparing for war, but they want to use the guise of the League of Nations to better sway in front of the public, and it is more conducive to their own preparation for war (although this war is actively opposed by the public), and to obtain a more superior position in wartime in order to defeat the enemy.

Slowdown

— Chun Sheng

Streetwalker

In the weather of October, even in the temperate Eastern metropolis, the wind blowing on the body is strong enough. In the deep night, the wind blew even harder, tearing down the withered leaves on the trees on both sides of the road, blowing up the cheongsams of the goddesses standing on both sides of the road, and piercing the hearts of all the poor. This is a sharp knife of nature!

There are countless stars in the deep blue sky and sea, winking their eyebrows, as if also satirizing and mocking the contradictions of this metropolis. In the middle of the road, cars were constantly running one after another, with fat-bellied men and petite women sitting leisurely in the carriages, seeking their stimulation in large theaters, nightclubs, and dance halls. A group of people were active under the three major companies and the Great World. They seemed not to know that they should rest at night. Their faces were covered with a thick layer of powder, their cheeks and lips were smeared with red rouge, and they smelled of inferior viewing water. There were old women with wrinkles all over their foreheads and young girls who had not yet fully developed. They were densely and tightly squeezed on both sides of the road, reaching out their hands to grab one or two workers, students, or country bumpkins, and exchange their bodies for living materials. Perhaps because of the tight wind and the thin clothes on their bodies, their upper and lower teeth were hitting each other, their bodies were shivering, and their legs were shaking like ghosts.

Gui, she had not been doing this kind of life for long. Having endured the coercion of the knife-like wind and the whip-like gaze of the procuress, she was in so much pain that she wanted to cry, and warm memories slowly climbed into her heart.

It was also such a quiet silver night, and the strength of the wind was not worse than today, but she didn't feel cold. Her mother was sewing clothes under the dim yellow light, and my sister and I were playing hide-and-seek in the courtyard...

In front of her, the towering buildings and flashing red lights and the noise of the metropolis disappeared. The dim yellow light, her mother's kind face, her brother's mischief, the narrow courtyard paved with gravel... all these lovely memories were like little waves jumping in her mind, warming her heart, and she fell into contemplation.

[Pig ! Do you want to eat a living? People ran past you and you didn't see it!]

Timely Article

Chinese New Year

— Qin Youheng

Uncle Genshou came back and said, "People in the city are busy celebrating the New Year."

"New Year!" Lizhen was washing clothes in the hall. Hearing her father say this, she turned around in astonishment. "Today is only November 14th."

"How do you know if you're huddled at home? They're following foreign days outside." Uncle Genshou bent down to take off his straw sandals, which were covered in mud.

"What foreign days? Isn't that what the teacher in the foreign school said about the solar calendar?" Lizhen asked.

Uncle Genshou put down the trouser legs rolled up on his knees, wiped his mouth, and said, "What isn't? Damn it, country people suffer. Originally, it wouldn't be too late to pay the rent for rice at this time, but if they change this day, they'll roll their eyes and say it's overdue. Originally..."

Lizhen knew that her father had suffered again and returned. She went to the room behind the fence to get the water pipe. Unfortunately, there wasn't a single layer of water smoke, and she ran out empty-handed.

"Dad, didn't you bring back some water smoke when you went to the city?"

"I thought about it, but the shipping costs have increased and I'm afraid the travel expenses won't be enough. Fortunately, I don't want to smoke when I'm annoyed. Lizhen, this anger is really hard to bear. That guy who pestered you last time and was scolded away can't get along with me. He loudly told me to give up the field and let someone else plant it."

"Um, is that the one wearing the diagonal vest, the deputy bookkeeper of the Qin family?"

"That's him."

"It's better not to argue with him too much. I heard that he is Mrs. Qin's godson. What if he really takes the field?" Lizhen wiped the soap foam piled on her arm on the edge of the foot basin.

"Giving in to others is not something I can do, even if it means losing my head. They are happy, slaughtering pigs and sheep to celebrate the New Year. What do we get after working a season?"

"But we want to celebrate the Chinese New Year." Lizhen said coquettishly.

"No matter what year you celebrate, you have to have money. Like your mother helping people outside, the money she earns back home month after month is only enough to pay the interest. It's a pity that she's outside, but her heart is hanging at home, and she can't bear to part with you. The day before yesterday, she picked up a pair of broken socks while taking out the garbage, washed them clean, and told me to bring them to you to wear for the New Year."

As Uncle Genshou spoke, he took out a paper package from his arms and handed it to Lizhen.

Lizhen took it. "Will Mom come back for the New Year?"

Uncle Genshou's face sank. "I don't think she'll come back. She has to help the master's family with the New Year's affairs."

"Didn't you just say that people in the city celebrate the foreign New Year?"

"Alas, for people with money, every day is like the New Year. They wear good clothes and eat fatty food. What's the big deal with celebrating two New Years? Anyway, they like to make noise and have fun." As Uncle Genshou said this, the township chief sent someone to call him to apportion the river dredging donation.

Lizhen stared blankly at the paper package, and the kind face of her mother vaguely appeared before her eyes. But, mother, mother is helping her master's family celebrate the New Year.

The hall was still a deathly silent hall.

Outport Postal Agency

Child Gentlemen and Child Stars

— Metaphor for Young Children

Shanxi Fenyang Communication

Dear readers, in this extraordinary state of rural organization faltering and the economy on the verge of collapse, allow me to tell you about the state of rural children's education.

There are two places where rural children study and receive education: one is the private school in the village, and the other is the so-called "foreign school" in the town. I really don't understand why the villagers still call textbooks "foreign books" and county-run schools "foreign schools." And those teachers responsible for rural education are so muddleheaded that they let them call it that, filling the air with "foreign" sounds. Dear readers, who do you think is to blame?

However, there's no need to waste words on this. Now, let's talk about the reality of these two children's education institutions. Most private schools are set up in the gloomy ancestral halls. Families with children in the village pool together ten or twenty dollars and invite an old scholar from the late Qing dynasty to lock up a group of innocent and lively children, accompanying the teacher in a life sentence-like ordeal. Imagine how those wild horse-like children can endure this invisible shackle. The one-foot-long, one-and-a-half inch wide, two-tenths of an inch thick bamboo ruler on the teacher's desk is enough to scare them silly.

Often, a very active child becomes dull and wooden after entering a private school. The old scholar only believes in the principle of "enduring hardship to become a superior person," and scolds the children with an iron face all day long. How can he care whether the children's nature and nerves can withstand this sudden oppression and restraint?

There's also a joke: the child from Third Uncle's family, who is nine years old this year, can recite a "Three Character Classic" fluently. But when I wrote the character "善" (shan, good) from "性本善" (xing ben shan, human nature is good) on a piece of paper for him to recognize, he stared blankly and couldn't answer. This shows that studying in a private school is just rote memorization. The children fear the teacher's ruler, so they have to memorize to avoid getting hit on the palm. This kind of overly strict private school education is really not suitable for young rural children.

However, what about the schools? What are they like?

You may have seen the schools in the towns. That kind of crude and makeshift organization, those teachers who hold their positions without contributing (very few are truly responsible), that kind of laissez-faire education is not necessarily more optimistic than private schools. The day before yesterday afternoon, my younger brother Shenze invited me to go to town to play and visit the XX County Junior Primary School. It was really ridiculous. The teacher was blowing a whistle and teaching the children to sing "Meng Jiangnu Searching for Her Husband." I heard that they spend half the day on the playground (courtyard) and the other half on singing and dancing.

Dear readers, don't think I'm exaggerating. Aunt's son Zhendi is also studying there. He's been studying for two years and has just finished a primer. But his singing and dancing skills are indeed very impressive.

What good does this kind of laissez-faire education do for rural children?

In my opinion, rural children's education should not be too strict or too lenient. It's best to have a balance of strictness and leniency. At the same time, we shouldn't constantly introduce the various luxuries and pleasures of the city to them. We should always point out the position of farmers in society and the reasons why the countryside is in such a bad state. But these words shouldn't be spoken with the face of a "teacher." They should be phrased more subtly.

However, in a situation where the national political system is not on track, and on the one hand, we are busy with "internal pacification and external resistance," it is a common and inevitable trend that primary school teachers in the countryside cannot receive their salaries, and children in the countryside cannot receive a good education!

Amateur Studies

What is the Most Useful Knowledge?

— Ms. Song Lingyi

"To learn is to apply," although this is an ancient Chinese proverb, it has not lost its absolute correctness even now. People who study medicine and engineering naturally do so for "application." Those who study politics, law, philosophy, and literature are also inseparable from the word "application." Whether Watt invented the steam engine for "application" when he invented it doesn't matter, but it was ultimately "used" by the so-called "civilized society" of modern times. The Christian doctrine of "universal love" seems fair on the surface, but it has been "used" by imperialism. In short, no matter what knowledge, no matter what you learn, you can't leave the word "application." "To learn is to apply" is indeed a true and undeniable truth.

However, what is manifested in China today is either "learning without application" or "learning something different from what is applied." Generally, people with knowledge and talent don't have the opportunity to "apply" it. People who study science and engineering become political committee members. People who study medicine and agriculture become company accountants or tax office clerks. These are common phenomena in Chinese society today. Therefore, some sensitive people think that the saying "to learn is to apply" is wrong and that to learn true knowledge, one should break away from this useless word "application." Thus, the theories of "learning for the sake of learning" and "reading for the sake of reading" have been advocated.

In fact, the so-called phenomena of "learning without application" and "learning something different from what is applied" that are currently appearing are products of a deformed Chinese society. The fact that people who study science don't have the opportunity to use their scientific talents proves that the deformed Chinese society rejects science. This is not because the theory of "to learn is to apply" is wrong, but because there is a problem with Chinese society. In order to solve the problems of Chinese society, there is a greater need for knowledge that can solve these problems. If we ignore this and advocate "learning for the sake of learning" and "reading for the sake of reading," it will only prolong this deformed Chinese society, and the phenomena of "learning without application" and "learning something different from what is applied" produced by this society will become even more widespread. As for what "true" knowledge is, it will certainly not be produced, because knowledge is social, not super-social. The deformed Chinese society of today can never accommodate "true" knowledge. What it accommodates is only unhealthy and base knowledge.

Therefore, under the current circumstances, what we need to learn is not only the knowledge that is "useful," but also the knowledge that is the most "useful," which is the knowledge that can solve all the problems produced by the deformed Chinese society.

What kind of knowledge can solve the problems that are currently occurring in Chinese society? I don't have any specific opinions here. I only say that to solve all the problems of Chinese society, one must understand the actual economic and political situation in China. Therefore, those who seek the most useful knowledge must participate in all social movements and understand all social situations. The so-called methods of "reading behind closed doors" and "not discussing state affairs" are really concrete manifestations of a policy of fooling the people. As long as one is not willing to be manipulated by this policy, one will inevitably link theory with practice and strive to seek the most useful knowledge in light of the actual situation of Chinese society today.

A Small Social Model

Long-Term Trial

— Guan Ying

The Office

Finally, thanks to the blessings of heaven, I finally found a position with my own pen in the midst of the thousands of unemployed people. I have been working for three or four months now, and it's even in a company office! Speaking of offices, they are also divided into many levels. Some are magnificent foreign houses, and some only rent a room. The staff inside, some earn hundreds of taels a month, which is very common, while others earn at most ten dollars a month, which is not even as good as a doorman. The office where I work is in a corner on the second floor of an old foreign house that is at least half a century old. The staircase is as dark as night even in the daytime, and there isn't even a street light. When going up and down, one has to be careful to avoid falling. Two dimly lit inner rooms are where we work. However, although the place is small, its function is great. As long as you count the signs on the wall when you enter, there are at least ten or twenty of them, such as XX Association, XX Society, XX Hall, which will make you confused about what kind of organization it is.

I remember it was when summer was turning to autumn when I was looking for a job. Suddenly, I received a reply to my unsolicited application, asking me to discuss everything in person.

How happy I was at that time! I went to XX Company—the company I now work for—with the letter that I had obtained like a treasure, to meet the manager. After an interview, he was satisfied with me and asked me to start by handling documents. The trial period was three months, with a monthly allowance of ten dollars for transportation. After the trial period, if I was suitable, my monthly salary would start at twenty-five dollars, and the trial period could be shortened. Although I thought the salary was too low at the time and not enough to cover the minimum cost of living, I was willing to do it with peace of mind because the prospects were good. When I first started, I was indeed only doing document work. I had to write at least dozens of letters every day. Fortunately, I had some training in writing, so I was able to handle it with ease. Later, I don't know how they found out that I also knew a little about accounting, so they slowly assigned me most of the accounting books. I thought that during the trial period, I might as well show off my skills, so I was happy to do my best. But, this way, it was terrible! From morning to night, except for a moment of leisure during meals, I was burying myself in my desk, working non-stop.

One month, two months... Time flew by like a galloping horse. This heavy work had worn me out. My glimmer of hope was tied to the formal employment after the trial period! The salary increase issue. This was my only hope and comfort. I had publicly expressed it in conversations with friends and in letters I sent back home. They were all envious and looking forward to my bright future and stable life. I was also confident that my performance during the trial period was not bad, and that this goal could be achieved.

At the end of the third month, he didn't say a word to me. Of course, I continued to work, thinking that not being fired meant I was suitable. Since I was formally employed, the minimum salary—twenty-five dollars—was definitely mine. I was happy, I was excited, and another month passed quickly. One day, just as I was about to leave the office, the manager called me over. I knew it was time to get paid, and my heart was pounding. As soon as we met, he first said a lot about how sluggish business was, and finally added, "I can only pay you this amount." As he spoke, he handed over two five-dollar bills and two white-silver Yuan coins. When I heard these words and saw this amount, I felt like I had been electrocuted, numb. I wanted to say something, but he had already stood up to answer the phone. My God! What to say? What's the use of saying anything? Unless you quit. If you don't quit, in this depressed year, there are many people who are willing to sell themselves cheap.

I took the twelve-dollar salary and walked out of the company gate. The city's torches illuminated the darkness. The cold wind of the night slapped my face like a knife, filled with endless threats. The dream of hope had been shattered.

Female Worker

— Mu Zeqing

The electric light is bright when I get up in the morning,

The electric light is dim when I return at night.

I look at the electric light morning and evening,

But it's the electric light that's looking at me!

X X X

The electric light shines on the open dam,

Shining on my way home and away.

When I return home and leave,

My daughter keeps calling "Mommy!"

X X X

Mommy returns with empty hands,

Empties her hands to hug her daughter.

"Darling, don't cry so loud,

Mommy is very worried today!"

X X X

"Darling, don't cry so loud,

Wait a while and Daddy will come home.

Wait a while and Daddy will come home,

He'll buy cakes and pastries for Darling!"

X X X

"Darling, don't cry so loud,

Quick, look at the electric light blooming red flowers,

One, two, three, four flowers,

Blooming all over the sky immediately!"

Occupational Anecdotes

Self-Esteem and Occupation

— Xing Jian

Here are two positions: one is the so-called quasi-voluntary teacher that is often advertised in newspapers, with a monthly allowance of eight dollars for transportation and accommodation at one's own expense; the other is a tea server, with a monthly salary of fifteen dollars, including food and lodging. I think that except for those who are illiterate and can only be tea servers, anyone who has studied for a few years and is qualified to be a teacher would definitely choose the first position. Money is something that everyone only complains about being too little, not too much, especially those unemployed people who can use an extra copper coin to solve an already meager living (of course, there are some exceptions, but I think most are like this). But why do they prefer to choose the first position with a lower salary and poorer treatment? In a word, it is "self-esteem" that is at work. Here are two examples:

I have a friend who graduated from middle school. Because of financial problems, he couldn't afford to pursue further education and had to wait at home for the opportunity to enter society. Although his knowledge is not bad, first, he lacks recommendations, and second, he is full of history, geography, geometry, and trigonometry, and has almost no business experience. One year, two years, slipped by in the blink of an eye, and he was still sitting at home as a parasite. Once, because he couldn't bear the pressure of life, it just so happened that a relative said he would introduce him to a store department to be a trainee. He went there with a thick skin (as he himself said) and came back after three days, saying he wouldn't do it anymore. He said angrily, "[...] In addition to the physical labor of being busy from seven o'clock in the morning to ten o'clock at night, almost without time to eat or relieve himself, he also had to watch the faces of the senior staff. For me, a respectable (?) middle school graduate, to do this menial work and have to put up with bad temper, I would rather tighten my belt and starve to death than do it [...]." When I heard this, apart from sighing helplessly, I felt that his self-esteem was at play.

Another friend who didn't graduate from middle school also wanted to enter society due to economic pressure. But there were always a few people with the same knowledge and situation as him that could be found everywhere in society. Although he tried his best and spent a lot of hard-earned postage, three years passed in the blink of an eye, and he still couldn't grab a broken job. A friend of his knew two bosses who sold English newspapers wholesale. According to the boss, he sold the newspapers to the hawkers for eight cents, and the hawkers could sell them for ten cents, earning two cents per copy. If they could sell forty copies a day (which is the most common sales volume), they would have eight jiao of income. Also, Westerners often give two jiao without asking for change, which is "extra money." So, making a dollar or more a day is very common. His friend wanted to introduce him to try selling newspapers, but he declined because he didn't want to embarrass his father. But no matter what, I think the motivation for his refusal had some element of self-esteem mixed in.

Thousands upon thousands of unemployed people are stretching out their hands to society for bread, and many, many unemployed people are committing suicide due to economic pressure. Although most of it is due to the economic recession, I dare to assert that a lot of the responsibility should be borne by self-esteem.

Finally, we shout out loud:

[Earning a living by labor is the same as earning a living by knowledge. It is not embarrassing, let alone a disgrace.

Down with the ethereal, harmful, and useless self-esteem!]

Special Collision Self-Employment Introduction

Model

— Qiu Yiqin

I have been looking for work for four months, which adds up to more than two hundred days. Even now, I haven't even seen a glimmer of hope! Although the extremely serious life of [hunger and cold] is still pressing me tightly.

I accidentally looked in the mirror, which couldn't help but make me extremely angry and sad. From my small and dark eyes, it fully shows that I am already exhausted. A yellow-black face as gloomy as a wax museum model naturally doesn't have a trace of a smile. Below the unkempt and greasy hair is my mouth, which needs a lot of bread stuffed into it every day. Besides, I have nothing! To be precise... I am just a breathing skeleton and a blood-and-tears-soaked zombie!

Of course, if it weren't for the struggle for this miserable [life], who in this world would be willing to linger forever? After I have endured the [scorn], [ridicule], [insult], [pain] of life!

In the past, I had bravely wanted to kill my future from the hail of bullets. So, I generously drove my whole body and child consciousness into the generally disciplined army life. But I didn't... In several charges, I didn't expose my bones to the sand and gravel to be a loyal and righteous wronged soul! When I quietly crawled up from the extremely tired and bloody ground, I looked around at my surroundings, which were filled with no breath of life. I was at a loss as to who I was fighting for? Who was I sacrificing for? Not only did I not find the future I was looking for here, but because several dear brothers in arms had died one after another, it further increased my infinitely deep sorrow, so I returned to my hometown in dismay!

In order to live to survive, I have to find bread myself, once or twice, and now it seems that I am exhausted and dull. [Hunger] and [cold] drive me to beg the gentlemen of this newspaper. If there is still a bit of compassionate sympathy in this world, at least I believe I will not be completely desperate. Although I don't have any special skills, I have also done many times the work of saving members, librarians, reporters, and painters. I am now in urgent need of work similar to the above to exchange for my minimum price. Correspondence to this publication.

Industrial and Commercial Research

My Opinion on Improving Chinese Bookkeeping

— Ju Fu

Improving Chinese bookkeeping has been heavily promoted. I studied accounting, bookkeeping, and other subjects in school, and my current job is as an accountant, so I naturally pay attention to this matter. Now, I will briefly write down what I have learned from this research.

First, there is the problem of separating the columns for the number of amounts. The amount columns of double-entry bookkeeping clearly separate the columns for ten thousands, thousands, hundreds, tens, yuan, jiao, and fen, etc., and the columns between thousands and hundreds are separated by a dark blue line, and the columns between yuan and jiao are separated by a red line to show conspicuousness. Now, the amount columns of improved Chinese bookkeeping are not clearly separated, and they are the same as those that are not improved. In this way, one ten thousand yuan and one hundred yuan both have three characters, and five yuan and five fen both have two characters. How can this be clear at a glance? It does not meet the purpose of accounting to be clear! If we can print lines and separate the columns according to double-entry bookkeeping, then one ten thousand yuan, including two decimal places, occupies seven spaces, one hundred yuan, including two decimal places, occupies five spaces, and these five spaces are all after the dark blue line. Five yuan, including two decimal places, occupies three spaces, and five fen occupies one space, and this space is after the red line. With the above method of recording, the numbers have different lengths and different positions, so of course it is clear at a glance to know their size, and there will be no confusion. The amount is the most important part of the ledger. Since it is called improvement, this point should not be ignored.

Second, there is the issue of horizontal and vertical formats. Vertical format must use vertical paper, and vertical paper should not be too long, which is not convenient for setting up multiple amount columns. Horizontal format can adopt the multi-column accounting method. The multi-column accounting method is very convenient and has the functions of differentiation and aggregation. Because the multi-column accounting method is to collect all accounts in one ledger, the entire record is in sight. Both recording and checking accounts can avoid turning over and checking here and there, which can avoid a lot of trouble, save a lot of time, and reduce a lot of mental effort. Moreover, collecting all accounts in one ledger will of course use fewer books. If you use a vertical format, it will be counterproductive! Therefore, this point is worth discussing, and we must not think that the system passed down for thousands of years is the most precious and supreme national essence!

Third, there is the question of what kind of numerals to use for accounting. Everyone knows that Arabic numerals have been used by all countries in the world. Even in our country, from university professors to male and female workers, everyone knows them. Now, house numbers, cars, and other numbers are also used, which shows that Arabic numerals are already very common in China. Moreover, schools across the country, from primary schools, order children to learn Arabic numerals. In the future, Arabic numerals in China will undoubtedly be adopted everywhere, just like in other countries in the world. Therefore, I think that Arabic numerals should be used for accounting. Arabic numerals are suitable for horizontal writing, which shows that horizontal bookkeeping is suitable for adoption. In fact, our people can be said to be accustomed to looking at numbers horizontally, because the numbers represented by the abacus, which has been used by the business community for thousands of years, are arranged in the same way as Arabic numerals, which is completely horizontal.

Someone said, "[According to your proposal, then what about writing with a brush? What about writing with a fountain pen? What about using foreign paper? What about using domestic paper?]" Here I can add a few words: the ledger is very important. The law clearly stipulates that it must be kept for ten years, which shows that the paper must be strong and not easily broken. Try to see the cash receipt and transfer voucher. The first step is to go through the form maker, accountant, and approver, and then transfer it to record the various accounts, which must go through several transfers. If the paper is soft and thin, will it not break? Someone said, "[Then domestic products are not good?]" I think domestic products should of course be promoted. Is there any objection to making money yourself? But blindly sticking to the old methods and not knowing how to improve, imitate, and create is really not a positive method! Can we walk long distances because there are no domestic trains? Cutting your feet to fit your shoes or giving up eating because of choking is not a long-term solution after all! Schools across the country use no small number of fountain pens and foreign paper. If we can make them ourselves and recover our rights, it will not be insignificant!

Finally, I have a few words about the book [An Outline of Improved Chinese Bookkeeping]. It says, "Chinese bookkeeping... accounting personnel are easy to obtain, unlike Western bookkeeping... it is difficult to obtain talents, and expenses must be increased everywhere." (See page 2 of the book) It also says, "Improved Chinese bookkeeping... talents and supplies can be obtained at a lower price..." (See page 4 of the book) But it itself says, "Improved Chinese bookkeeping is a bookkeeping method that uses the latest theories." (See page 5 of the book) The author of the book also said in his article [The Four Periods of Improved Chinese Bookkeeping] that his improved Chinese bookkeeping "is no less interconnected in principle than Western double-entry bookkeeping," and also said that it "has never deviated from the principles of double-entry bookkeeping" (see the Shenbao Economic Special Edition of December 15). This shows that the principles of improved Chinese bookkeeping and Western double-entry bookkeeping are the same. Then, to understand the principles of accounting, whether it is improved Chinese bookkeeping or Western double-entry bookkeeping, you undoubtedly need to study and understand the principles. Since this is the case, then I would like to ask... why is it easy to obtain Chinese bookkeepers, but difficult to obtain Western bookkeepers? Is this statement specifically used to explain that the price of Chinese bookkeepers should be cheaper, while the price of Western bookkeepers is too expensive, and that you have to increase expenses everywhere? This statement really has the intention of promoting capital to reduce the wages of labor! This intention may please the capital side, but we people who work hard day and night must raise a serious protest!
